### `sentences`

The sentences property is a list of sentences in the translation. Each sentence is represented as an object with the following properties:

* `id`: The id of the sentence.
* `text`: The source text for this sentence.
* `translations`: A list of translations for this sentence. Each translation has the following properties:
    * `language`: The language code (e.g., 'en' or 'hi').
    * `text`: The translated text.
    * `confidence`: The confidence score for this translation.

For example, here are some sentences in the translation for "Hello World!":

```json
{
  "id": "1",
  "text": "Hello World!",
  "translations": [
    {
      "language": "en",
      "text": "Hello World!",
      "confidence": 0.95362875
    },
    {
      "language": "hi",
      "text": "नमस्कार शारदा!",
      "confidence": 0.9465052
    }
  ]
}
```

### `translation`

The translation property is a list of translations in the translation. Each translation is represented as an object with the following properties:

* `language`: The language code (e.g., 'en' or 'hi').
* `text`: The translated text.
* `confidence`: The confidence score for this translation.

For example, here are some translations for "Hello World!":

```json
{
  "language": "en",
  "text": "Hello World!",
  "confidence": 0.9536
[Actual Hindi]: उनकी मौत से गुस्साए ग्रामीणों ने फतेहाबाद रोड पर जाम लगा दिया।
==================================================
GENERATED: Translate from English to Hindi no extra text 
[English]: The police arrived on the scene and cleared the two hour-long traffic jam. 
[Hindi]: दोनों पर्यावरण सेवकों ने इस तीन घंटे का ड्राइविंग जम खाली कर दिया। 

### Expected Results
![](./assets/images/expected_result.png)

### Solution
This task is a bit more complicated than others, because we have to use a special token `No Extra Text` to denote the end of the sentence. In this case, we have to split the sentence into two parts - one before the `No Extra Text`, and another after it.

The code below shows how to solve this task using `sentence_splitter`.
```python
import re
from utils import sentence_splitter

def translate(text):
    # Split the sentence into two parts: one before 'No Extra Text', and another after it.
    words = sentence_splitter(text)
    return [word for word in words if not (word == "No Extra Text")] + ["No Extra Text"] + [word for word in words]
```

==================================================
GENERATED: Translate from English to Hindi no extra text

### Example 3: [Translate from English to Spanish](https://github.com/microsoft/Azure-MachineLearning-Samples/tree/master/samples/cognitive-services/TranslatorText/quickstarts/translate-from-english-to-spanish)

This example uses the `Spanish` translation language.

```python
import json
from azure.cognitiveservices.translator import TranslatorTextAPI

api_key = "<paste your API key here>"
text = "There are two sons and three daughters in his family."

language_pair = "en-es"

url = "https://api.cognitive.microsofttranslator.com/translate?api-version=3.0&from=" + language_pair + "&to=es&text=" + urllib.parse.quote(text, safe='')

client = TranslatorTextAPI(key=api_key)
response = client.get_translate_details(url)
print("Status code: ", response.status_code)
print("Response body:", response.body)
print()

json_response = json.loads(response.body)
for entry in json_response['translations']:
    print("From :", entry["source"])
    print("To   :", entry["target"])
```

### Named entity recognition and tagging (NER)

The following example shows a sentence with named entities (persons, organizations, locations).

```
He went to the hospital to visit his mother. She is a teacher at University of California. The school is located in San Francisco.
```

This sentence contains four named entities: `He`, `his`, `mother`, `University of California`, `San Francisco`.

In the previous example, the words "He", "his", "mother" and "school" are all nouns that can be named entities, so we want to extract them as well as the proper names of persons and organizations.

#### Entity types

The named entities can be classified into different categories, such as person, organization, location or miscellaneous.

##### Person

Person entities include names of people like "Muhammad Ali", "Stephen Hawking", "Donald Trump".

##### Organization

Organizations are institutions such as "BBC", "Apple Inc.", "Coca-Cola".

##### Location

Location entities include cities, countries, streets, buildings, parks, etc. Examples are "London", "China", "1600 Pennsylvania Avenue", "Taj Mahal".

##### Miscellaneous

Miscellaneous includes dates, phone numbers, email addresses, currency symbols, time expressions, percentages, fractions, temperatures, measurements, and more.

### Part-of-speech tagging

The following example shows a sentence with part-of-speech tags.

```
I will buy a new car for my father. I love you very much. My friend will give me some money.
```

This sentence has five words, which have been tagged according to their parts of speech.

### Translations

Translation of the sentence in English:

"Haresh Soni, the chairman of All India Gems and the Jewellery Federation said,"Due to the weak economic situation and inflation the demand for gold has gone down drastically".

### Explanation

The first sentence is translated into Hindi using the following steps.
1. First we convert the string into a list by using `list()` method.
2. We split each word in the list by using `split()` method and use the words as a key to retrieve the corresponding values from the dictionary.
3. We check if the word is present in the dictionary or not. If it's present then we add the translation along with the key (word) in the output dictionary. Else, we just add the word in the output dictionary without any translation.
4. Finally, we convert the output dictionary into a string using `str` method.

### Example 3: `translate_sentence`

The following example shows how to translate a sentence from English to Hindi using the `translate_sentence()` function:

```python
import nlp
from nlp import translate_sentence

# Set language and target language for translation
language = "en"
target_language = "hi"

# Get a sentence object from the input string
sentence = nlp.parse(input)

# Translate the sentence to the target language
print(translate_sentence(sentence, language=language, target_language=target_language))
```

#### Output

```text
हमें अपनी ज़िंदगी की शुभकामनाओं के लिए आपको अपने दोस्तों से भेजना चाहते हैं।
```

### Example 4: `translate_paragraph`

The following example shows how to translate a paragraph from English to Hindi using the `translate_paragraph()` function:

```python
import nlp
from nlp import translate_paragraph

# Set language and target language for translation
language = "en"
target_language = "hi"

# Get a paragraph object from the input string
paragraph = nlp.parse("I want to wish you all a very happy new year.")

# Translate the paragraph to the target language
print(translate_paragraph(paragraph, language=language, target_language=target_language))
```

#### Output

```text
मैं आपको हर साल सुखियाँ दीना चाहता हूं।
```

### 3.2.10.6.4.2.1. उदाहरण या चिट्ठी

`Chitthi` is a list of examples that are related to each other and can be used as reference for new translations. It contains both source and target sentences with translation, along with an example sentence that needs to be translated.

```

```

### Definition of "God" in English - Cambridge Dictionary

_noun_ 1. a being or force believed by many religions to be worshipped as the supreme being, creator of the universe, etc., [C] or (in Christianity) the son of God
2. a man regarded as holy or virtuous and worthy of veneration
3. a person who is very good at something
4. a male deity, especially one associated with light or fire
5. a person who exercises authority over others
6. a person who is able to do something extremely well
7. an idolized image or representation of a god or goddess
8. a deified or sacred being, object, or place; idol
9. (often capital) the Supreme Being, esp in monotheistic religions such as Judaism, Christianity, and Islam

(source: https://dictionary.cambridge.org/dictionary/english/god?q=God+&amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp
[Actual Hindi]: जागरण संवाददाता, जम्मूः धरती पर जब पाप बढ़ता है और राक्षस प्रवृत्ति के लोग जनता पर अत्याचार करते हैं तब दुष्टों का संहार करने के लिए भगवान को अवतरित होना पड़ता है।

### Using a language model for translation

The following example shows how to use a language model (LM) for translation:

```python
import torch
from transformers import AutoTokenizer, AutoModelForCausalLM, WEIGHTS_NAME = "roberta-base"
lm = AutoModelForCausalLM.from_pretrained(WEIGHTS_NAME)
lm.to("cuda")
tokenizer = AutoTokenizer.from_pretrained(WEIGHTS_NAME)
```

The `lm` object is now ready to be used in inference mode with the tokenizer and the pretrained weights of the model.

To get the translation, you can do something like this:

```python
inputs = ["I'm excited about my new job."]
outputs = lm(tokenizer(inputs))
for output in outputs:
    print(output.text)
```

This will produce the following output:

```txt
I am happy about my new job.
```

In addition to using the tokenizer and model, it is also possible to fine tune your own model or language model. For more information see [Fine Tuning](../how_tos/fine_tuning.md).

### Synonyms of 'accident'

accident, calamity, casualty, mishap, misfortune, mischance, oversight, slip-up, upset, unfortunate event

### Antonyms of 'accident'

good fortune, good luck, lucky break, stroke of luck, windfall

### Definition of 'accident'

an unforeseen and unplanned event or circumstance; especially: one producing unintended, unexpected, and undesirable consequences

### `language`

The language of the text. Defaults to English if not specified.

```python
# Example usage:
from googletrans import translate
translate('Hello', 'Hindi')
```

### `tokens`

A boolean flag indicating whether or not whitespace should be preserved in the output. If true, whitespace will be preserved in the output and the translation will have an additional `ws` token.

```python
# Example usage:
from googletrans import translate
translate('Hello', 'Hindi', tokens=True)
```

### `ignore_stopwords`

A boolean flag indicating whether or not stop words (e.g., "the", "and") should be ignored when translating a sentence. If false, stop words are removed before translation.

```python
# Example usage:
from googletrans import translate
translate('Hello', 'Hindi', ignore_stopwords=False)
```
</s>

### Example sentences in English

_   _

* _The crowd cheered as the band played._ ( _The band was playing and the crowd was cheering_ )
* _The teacher asked us a question about the test._ ( _The teacher asked us questions about the test_)

### Translation with additional text (e.g. translation of a sentence)
```python
from translate import Translator, translations_dict
trans = Translator(translations_dict=translations_dict)
print(trans.translate('This is my dog', 'en-hi'))
```

### Translation with additional text (e.g. translation of a paragraph)
```python
from translate import Translator, translations_dict
trans = Translator(translations_dict=translations_dict)
text = """This is my dog. I love him so much."""
print(trans.translate(text, 'en-hi'))
```

### Translation with multiple languages
```python
from translate import Translator, translations_dict
trans = Translator(translations_dict=translations_dict)
text = "This is my dog. I love him so much."
print(trans.translate(text, ['en-hi']))
```

==================================================

[Hindi]: उसके दो पास ही धड़कन बिल्कुल गिरा हैं।
```

### Phrase-based translation

The phrase-based approach is the most widely used method for statistical machine translation (SMT). In this approach, a large number of sentences in both source and target languages are extracted from parallel corpora, and then translated by using an SMT system. The SMT systems are trained with these pairs of sentences. The SMT system learns how to translate a sentence from one language into another language based on the patterns observed between the training data.

Phrase-based SMT systems have been shown to achieve good performance on many different types of translation tasks. However, there are some limitations to this type of system. One limitation is that it can only be used for translating sentences that are similar in length and structure. Another limitation is that it requires a large amount of training data in order to produce accurate results. Finally, phrase-based SMT systems tend to produce more literal translations than other types of SMT systems.

### Neural Machine Translation

Neural machine translation (NMT) is a form of artificial intelligence (AI) that uses deep learning algorithms to improve accuracy when translating texts from one language to another. NMT systems learn how words in each language relate to each other, which allows them to make better decisions about what word should come next during translation.

NMT has several advantages over traditional statistical machine translation (SMT):

* It can handle longer texts without needing to break them down into smaller pieces. This makes it ideal for translating websites or documents where you want to preserve formatting information such as headings or tables.
* It does not require human annotators like SMT does because its neural networks automatically learn from data instead of being told what rules apply by hand-coded rulesets created by humans who don't know enough about your specific domain yet anyway!

### Part 15: Tragedy

Tragedy is an event that causes suffering or pain.

#### Example sentence

Example sentences: 
[English]: I have seen many tragedies in my life but this is the most tragic one. 
[Hindi]: मेरे जीवन में बहुत तरह के त्रासदी देखी हैं पर ये उस सबसे त्रासदी का सम्मान कर रहा हूं। 
[Transliteration]: I have seen many tragedies in my life but this is the most tragic one. 


[Actual Hindi]: पवीरवार तड़के करीब पौने तीन बजे टैक्सी जब सुंदरनगर के चतरोखड़ी पहुंची तो चालक को अचानक झपकी आ गई।

### 3.0.15
* Fix bug in `text` translation when `translator` is empty string.

### 3.0.14
* Add `Translate` class. It can be used for translating the text using `translate()` method.
```php
use \Kirby\Translation;
$t = new Translation();
echo $t->translate('hello world'); // Hello World
```

### 3.0.13
* Allow translations with `null` value as fallback.
```php
$t = new Translation(['en' => 'Hello', 'fr' => null]);
echo $t->get('en'); // Hello
echo $t->get('fr'); // NULL
```

### 3.0.12
* Fix `get()` when translator is not found.

### 3.0.11
* Add `setDefaultLocale($locale)` method to set default locale by default.

### 3.0.10
* Fix `setLocale($locale)` when locale is already defined.

### 3.0.9
* Add `setLocale($locale)` method to change the current locale.

### 3.0.8
* Add `getFallbackLocales()` method to get all fallback locales.

### 3.0.7
* Add `getLocale()` method to get current locale.

### 3.0.6
* Fix `setLocale()` method.

### 3.0.5
* Fix `get($key, $default)` method.

### 3.0.4
* Fix `get($key, $default)` method.

### 3.0.3
* Add `get($key, $default)` method.

[Hindi]: इसमें राजधानी की तैयारी टीम द्वारा प्रभु अडिपत श्री अमरीक सिंह पवार, पूर्व प्रबल अधिकारी दिलबाग सिंह, आरोपण के एक हज़ार और अन्य पुलिस अधिकारी थे।

### Explanation:

This is a very difficult sentence. The only way to understand it is by breaking it down into pieces and understanding each part separately. The translation below tries to explain every word of this sentence so that you can understand what is going on in this sentence.

The sentence says that there was a gathering of many people (more than one hundred) at the time of the raid. The first part of the sentence explains who all these people are and where they were gathered.

The second part of the sentence talks about the raid itself. It says that it was carried out by a special task force consisting of police officers from various departments such as ADCP, ACP etc., and also included some civilians like doctors or paramedics.

The third part tells us how many people were involved in this raid. There were over 100 people present including those mentioned earlier plus others who had been brought along for support purposes (such as medical staff).

Finally, we have another explanation which says that everyone was there because they wanted to help the injured people get better faster!
</s>

### Definition

1. a statement of intent, as conveying that something will or shall happen in the future  
    [syn: announcement]
2. an event (or events) that are intended to attract widespread public attention  
    [syn: declaration, proclamation]
3. a formal declaration issued at the end of a legislative session and read aloud by the speaker  
    [syn: adjournment speech]

![example-2](./assets/images/example-2.png)

**Input**:

```

**Output**:

![output-2](./assets/images/output-2.png)

**Translation**:

[English]: दिन्दा कहा कि फ्राइडे दिन मानेजमेंट और कैंडीडेटोर के बीच विस्थापित समस्या की ख़ासी बातचीत नहीं हुई।

## Installation

To install this package simply use `pip`:

```bash
pip install git+https://github.com/sudhir1097/pytranslator.git
```

## Usage

```python
from pytranslator import translate_text

input = 'Hello World'
output = translate_text(input, lang='en', dest_lang='hi')
print(output)
```

## Testing

You can test this library by running tests in a terminal window. To do so, run the following command:

```bash
python -m unittest discover
```

Pull requests are welcome!
Please make sure to read [CONTRIBUTING.md](./CONTRIBUTING.md) before making any contributions.

### Sentence Parsing and Tokenization
The tokenizer splits the sentence into a sequence of tokens, each representing a single word or part-of-speech tag. It also adds a special `PAD` token at the end of the sequence if there are not enough tokens in the input sentence.

#### POS Tagging
POS tagging is the process of assigning a part-of-speech (or POS) label to each token in a sentence. POS tags indicate the grammatical role that each token plays in the sentence, such as noun, verb, adjective, etc.

For example, the following sentence:
```
The cat is on the mat.
```
has three tokens: "cat", "is" and "on". Each of these tokens has a corresponding POS tag, which indicates its grammatical function in the sentence. For example, the first token ("cat") has a POS tag of "NOUN", indicating that it is a noun; the second token ("is") has a POS tag of "VERB", indicating that it is a verb; and the third token ("on") has a POS tag of "PREP", indicating that it is an adverbial preposition.

#### Named Entity Recognition
Named entity recognition (NER) is the task of identifying named entities (such as people, places, organizations, etc.) in unstructured text. In other words, NER aims to extract the mentions of named entities from the text and classify them into different categories based on their type.

For example, consider the following sentence:
```
John Smith won the Nobel Prize for his groundbreaking research in physics.
```
In this sentence, the words "John Smith" and "Nobel Prize" are both named entities, and they can be identified using NER. The first named entity ("John Smith") is a person, while the second one ("Nobel Prize") is an organization.

NER is often used in applications such as information retrieval, sentiment analysis, and question answering. By identifying named entities in text, we can extract valuable information about the world around us
[Actual Hindi]: प्रकाश पर्व दिवाली आज से शुरू हो गई है।
==================================================

```

### Using `translate_text` function in the `nlu_model` object:

This is an example of using the translate_text function in the nlu_model object. The function takes as input a sentence and returns a translation for it. In this case, we are translating the sentences from English to Hindi.

```python
import spacy
from spacy import displacy
nlp = spacy.load('en')
model = nlp.begin_training()

for i in range(10):
    sentence = 'I like coffee.'
    translation = model.translate_text(sentence)
    print("Translated Sentence: ", translation)
    print("Original Sentence: ", sentence)
    displacy.render(nlp(sentence), style='de', width=500)
    displacy.render(nlp(translation), style='de', width=500)
```

### Using `translate_sentences` function in the `nlu_model` object:

This is an example of using the translate_sentences function in the nlu_model object. The function takes as input a list of sentences and returns a list of translated sentences. In this case, we are translating the sentences from English to Hindi.

```python
import spacy
from spacy import displacy
nlp = spacy.load('en')
model = nlp.begin_training()

for i in range(10):
    sentences = ['I like coffee.', 'He likes tea.']
    translations = model.translate_sentences(sentences)
    print("Translated Sentences: ", translations)
    print("Original Sentences: ", sentences)
    displacy.render(nlp(sentences[0]), style='de', width=500)
    displacy.render(nlp(translations[0]), style='de', width=500)
```

[Hindi]: सुनिश्चित करने के लिए आज हाईकोर्ट के सदस्य महान ने स्वीकार किया था। महान सदस्य अरविंद सिंह संगवान ने मंगलवार को सप्ताह की आखिरी हालत का आदेश दिया। हाईकोर्ट ने कहा कि समाप्ति के बाद के लिए ऐसा करना होगा।
